<div id="review_694166917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694166917" />
    <a title="Paul Bartusiak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10982623-paul-bartusiak"><img alt="Paul Bartusiak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345837119p2/10982623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694166917?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Bartusiak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Bartusiak" href="/user/show/10982623-paul-bartusiak">Paul Bartusiak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694166917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10360866353084430432">A paperback copy of <b>The Odessa File</b> has been sitting on my bookshelf for probably fifteen years; I can’t even remember anymore how I originally obtained it- probably at a used book sale (I always jump at the chance of picking up spy novels from some of the masters of the genre). There was a hesitance to read it for a long time (obviously), and I’m not really sure why. I think it must have been because for some reason I kept confusing it with the movie version of Ira Levin’s <b>The Boys from Brazil </b></span>
  <span id="freeText10360866353084430432" style="display:none">A paperback copy of <b>The Odessa File</b> has been sitting on my bookshelf for probably fifteen years; I can’t even remember anymore how I originally obtained it- probably at a used book sale (I always jump at the chance of picking up spy novels from some of the masters of the genre). There was a hesitance to read it for a long time (obviously), and I’m not really sure why. I think it must have been because for some reason I kept confusing it with the movie version of Ira Levin’s <b>The Boys from Brazil </b>that I saw a long time ago. After all, they’re both stories about post World War II and Nazi hunters. <br /><br />Well, I was finally in the mood to give it a try, and I’m really glad that I did! It became pretty clear to me that this was a story or movie that I had neither read nor seen before, and it was hard to put down once started. I finished it in just a few days, which is not easy for me given my hectic schedule. Forsyth has a great style, more direct that one of my favorites, John Le Carre, and he can really carry an emotional punch in just a few lines. There’s one passage that I won’t forget for a long time: <br /><br />“You’re from Buenos Aires?” he asked.<br />“No.”<br />“Where from, then?”<br />“Jerusalem.”<br /><br />Without knowing the context of this dialogue, one may not feel the tension in the lines, but in the context in the story, it was awesome. A writer only dreams of being able to convey such power in a scene while using such few, carefully chosen words. <br /><br />In brief summary, the main character, Peter Miller, is a sort of accomplished tabloid reporter. He chases an ambulance in Germany and arrives at a home where the resident, an old man, committed suicide. The police chief passes on to Miller the diary of the dead man, and this leads to an investigation and chase which is really quite fun to follow. <br /><br />I’ve read some other reviews that state this is not even close to being Forsyth’s best novel, and so I suppose I’ve got some great reading to look forward to. <b>The Day of the Jackal</b>, the original directed by Fred Zinnemann, is probably one of the best espionage/political thriller movies of all time, and I had the great pleasure of seeing it many times over during a period when film was front-and-center in my life, so I’ll put some of Forsyth’s other novels in line before that one, but it’s always great when one finally discovers such a great thriller writer, even if it did take several decades. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10360866353084430432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

He determines to track down "the butcher of Riga"-- a notorious Nazi responsible for thousands of deaths during World War II. His quest leads him to a sinister organization named Odessa. Taut, well written and suspenseful, this book is hard to put down.</span>

<div id="review_1088302398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088302398" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1088302398?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099559832" href="/book/show/10774517-the-odessa-file">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1088302398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2402277213610411589">Don’t you just hate it when you finally get to the good part of a book and then life gets really busy so you have to put it aside for a few days?<br/><br/>Sadly, such a thing is what happened with this one. Then, when I managed to get back to it I’d lost the small amount of love which had come about.<br/><br/>I should probably start by saying this is not a bad read. In so many ways it is really good – yet it did not push the right buttons for me. In my eyes too much of the story was lost to information being passed</span>
  <span id="freeText2402277213610411589" style="display:none">Don’t you just hate it when you finally get to the good part of a book and then life gets really busy so you have to put it aside for a few days?<br /><br />Sadly, such a thing is what happened with this one. Then, when I managed to get back to it I’d lost the small amount of love which had come about.<br /><br />I should probably start by saying this is not a bad read. In so many ways it is really good – yet it did not push the right buttons for me. In my eyes too much of the story was lost to information being passed on to us. There is nothing wrong with being given the information we receive in this book – it’s eye-opening and more people should give it a read for this very reason – but I felt as though this meant the actual story lost so much momentum. Moreover, I felt as though in some cases I was being told things that were pretty obvious to me. Such a thing may merely reflect my knowledge of the matters spoken about in this book, but to me it made it hard for me to get back into the actual story once we were done with the thirty page history essay.<br /><br />Speaking of the story, I felt as though the two different stories merely complicated issues. It was interesting the way that the two stories played together, yet one of the stories was given much more focus than the other so that when we came back to it we were just like ‘oh yeah, I almost forgot about this’. In short, there was not a very good matchup between the two stories being told.<br /><br />I also felt as though the characters were very one dimensional. Motives were really easy to work out and there was no real character development throughout. We were told what to think about people rather than being given the chance to form our own opinion. Even in the case of the main character there really wasn’t much to make him stand out.<br /><br />Overall an interesting story but it did not live up to expectations. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2402277213610411589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13324955138194851603"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423451352i/13627403._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='300' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I enjoyed that much of this thriller is spent on the German autobahns following the hero driving his 1960 Jaguar XK150 S at speeds over 100 mph. That car had about 250 HP, stiff peformance suspension, and a timeless design. He drove everywhere with it, through dark forests, blizzards, and to most of the major German cities. What fun it must be to do this! I have been encouraged finally to take a trip there and do the same...but without the snow.<br/><br/>On the negative side, Forsyth's second best known </span>
  <span id="freeText13324955138194851603" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423451352i/13627403._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I enjoyed that much of this thriller is spent on the German autobahns following the hero driving his 1960 Jaguar XK150 S at speeds over 100 mph. That car had about 250 HP, stiff peformance suspension, and a timeless design. He drove everywhere with it, through dark forests, blizzards, and to most of the major German cities. What fun it must be to do this! I have been encouraged finally to take a trip there and do the same...but without the snow.<br><br>On the negative side, Forsyth's second best known novel is a pedantic, cold, fictionalized historical "essay" that suffers from a lack of distinction between fact and invention. There is insufficient action and excitement to hide its underlying uninteresting mechanical structure. I was disappointed with the story...but the driving was great!<br><br> </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=l-nyt-bestsellers">l-nyt-bestsellers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=3-dnf">3-dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=f-kindle">f-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=sg-investigations">sg-investigations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=g-mystery">g-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=p5-wwii">p5-wwii</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078376297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9415140930461309630">I don't like the storytelling structure: Something happens, and then we get a huge historical background story. A new chapter starts, something else happens, and then we get another huge info dump. <br/><br/>If you can put up with this type of structure you will probably like it, but it's too tedious for me. I'm reading more <b>about</b> the story than I'm reading <b>of</b> the story. It's too bad, because the blurb makes it sound so much more interesting than it is.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2131150673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4472877115876568941">A great investigative romp through the German countryside in a very compelling and charming era. As always with Forsyth the depth of research and attention to detail is key.<br/><br/>Some dark moments without being self indulgent. The gradual rise in tension from start to finish is managed so carefully that you don't realise you're on the edge of your seat until almost toppling off.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2971981666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2971981666" />
    <a title="Priya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10460925-priya"><img alt="Priya" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2971981666?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Priya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Priya" href="/user/show/10460925-priya">Priya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099552819" href="/book/show/663370.The_Odessa_File">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2971981666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8785273028632049287">A young journalist is handed a diary of a dead Jew, who has written about his time when he was in the camps of the Nazi. The journalist then decides to track down the person responsible for thousands of deaths during the time. <br/>The research, background and plot of the book is very good. <br/>There is suspense, danger, action, drama and once the story gets going then it turns into a real page turner. <br/>A good time pass read!<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1395555939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395555939" />
    <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc"><img alt="RJ from the LBC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605827139p2/131730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395555939?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RJ from the LBC" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc">RJ from the LBC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131730-rj-from-the-lbc?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395555939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8724034293693681724">A secret organization comprised of former Nazi SS officers, plotting to deploy WMDs against Israel? That's heady stuff, especially 45 years ago when it was first published. Reporter Peter Miller is tracking a member of the shadowy Odessa organization but his motives remain unclear. Author Forsyth is known for meticulous plots that slowly build suspense, and this novel is no exception. Forsyth's characters don't normally make much of an impression but there's a riveting section late in the story </span>
  <span id="freeText8724034293693681724" style="display:none">A secret organization comprised of former Nazi SS officers, plotting to deploy WMDs against Israel? That's heady stuff, especially 45 years ago when it was first published. Reporter Peter Miller is tracking a member of the shadowy Odessa organization but his motives remain unclear. Author Forsyth is known for meticulous plots that slowly build suspense, and this novel is no exception. Forsyth's characters don't normally make much of an impression but there's a riveting section late in the story in which a Nazi officer indignantly defends his actions as the commandant of a concentration camp that is chilling to read. A few too many coincidences will make your eyes roll, and female characters are included for sex appeal only (ah, the 70s!) but the plot crashes inexorably forward like an out of control steamroller. As the Indiana Jones film franchise would later prove, Nazis make the best bad guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8724034293693681724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EVjfHJpt0HVz4z+bHtlmIO8/uj/wUWuoDRaygfrm72TlD2k4AsXWWrjxDSzW12W5xwEkywqI+EKWjMDSOLqF3w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0TmMCKOe4MkZeBtKJfu5HXiyfwMbsXQKsAsd8wwksdklbjosOzbm5tJqKf3t9bqEUIzh9+Fo5+ArkW+gznjbYg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36714.Frederick_Forsyth">About Frederick Forsyth</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/36714.Frederick_Forsyth"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1595729238p3/36714.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/36714.Frederick_Forsyth">Frederick Forsyth
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,751
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3645477885876731005">Frederick Forsyth, CBE is an English author and occasional political commentator. He is best known for thrillers such as <i>The Day of the Jackal</i>, <i>The Odessa File</i>, <i>The Fourth Protocol</i>, <i>The Dogs of War</i>, <i>The Devil's Alternative</i>, <i>The Fist of God</i>, <i>Icon</i>, <i>The Veteran</i>, <i>Avenger</i>, <i>The Afghan</i>, and recently <i>The Cobra</i> and <i>The Kill List</i>.<br/><br/>The son of a furrier, he was born in Ashford, Kent, educated at Tonbridge Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText3645477885876731005" style="display:none">Frederick Forsyth, CBE is an English author and occasional political commentator. He is best known for thrillers such as <i>The Day of the Jackal</i>, <i>The Odessa File</i>, <i>The Fourth Protocol</i>, <i>The Dogs of War</i>, <i>The Devil's Alternative</i>, <i>The Fist of God</i>, <i>Icon</i>, <i>The Veteran</i>, <i>Avenger</i>, <i>The Afghan</i>, and recently <i>The Cobra</i> and <i>The Kill List</i>.<br /><br />The son of a furrier, he was born in Ashford, Kent, educated at Tonbridge School and later attended the University of Granada. He became one of the youngest pilots in the Royal Air Force at 19, where he served on National Service from 1956 to 1958. Becoming a journalist, he joined Reuters in 1961 and later the BBC in 1965, where he served as an assistant diplomatic correspondent. From July to September 1967, he served as a correspondent covering the Nigerian Civil War between the region of Biafra and Nigeria. He left the BBC in 1968 after controversy arose over his alleged bias towards the Biafran cause and accusations that he falsified segments of his reports. Returning to Biafra as a freelance reporter, Forsyth wrote his first book, The Biafra Story in 1969.<br /><br />Forsyth decided to write a novel using similar research techniques to those used in journalism. His first full length novel, The Day of the Jackal, was published in 1971 and became an international bestseller and gained its author the Edgar Allan Poe Award for Best Novel. It was later made into a film of the same name.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3645477885876731005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
